end)</span>)</span></span></span></a></span></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#0079C1; color:#fff;">Location</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" Warwickshire">Rugby</a><br /> <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Loughborough" title="Loughborough">Loughborough</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Nottingham" </th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background:#0079C1; color:#fff;">Road network</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="hlist" style="text-align:center"><div class="hlist">
<ul><li><b><a href="/wiki/Roads_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Roads in the United Kingdom">Roads in the United Kingdom</a></b></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_motorways_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of motorways in the United Kingdom">Motorways</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_roads_zones_in_Great_Britain" title="List of roads zones in Great Britain">A and B road zones</a></li></ul></div>
<table style="width:100%; background:none; border-collapse:collapse"><tbody><tr><td style="text-align:left;padding:0;vertical-align:middle;width:45%">← <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/UK-Motorway-M1.svg/45px-UK-Motorway-M1.svg.png" decoding="async" width="45" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/UK-Motorway-M1.svg/68px-UK-Motorway-M1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/UK-Motorway-M1.svg/90px-UK-Motorway-M1.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="316" data-file-height="141" /> <span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-selflink selflink">M1</a></span></td><td style="text-align:center;width:10%;padding:0;vertical-align:middle;white-space:nowrap"></td><td style="text-align:right;padding:0;vertical-align:middle;width:45%"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/M2_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M2 motorway (Great Britain)">M2</a></span> <img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/UK-Motorway-M2.svg/45px-UK-Motorway-M2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="45" height="20" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/UK-Motorway-M2.svg/68px-UK-Motorway-M2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/UK-Motorway-M2.svg/90px-UK-Motorway-M2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="316" data-file-height="141" /> →</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>M1 motorway</b> connects <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> to <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a>, where it joins the <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1(M)</a> near <a href="/wiki/Aberford" title="Aberford">Aberford</a>, to connect to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>. It was the first inter-urban <a href="/wiki/Motorway" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway">motorway</a> to be completed in the UK;<sup id="cite_ref-archive_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> the first motorway in the country was the <a href="/wiki/Preston_By-pass" title="Preston By-pass">Preston By-pass</a>, which later became part of the <a href="/wiki/M6_motorway" title="M6 motorway">M6</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Highways_Agency_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highways_Agency-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Motorway" class="mw-redirect" title="Motorway">motorway</a> is 193 miles (311&#160;km) long and was constructed in four phases. Most of the motorway was opened between 1959 and 1968 but the southern end was extended in 1977 and the northern end was extended in 1999. It forms part of the unsigned <a href="/wiki/European_route_E13" title="European route E13">European route E13</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There had been plans before the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> for a motorway network in the United Kingdom. <a href="/wiki/John_Douglas-Scott-Montagu,_2nd_Baron_Montagu_of_Beaulieu" title="John Douglas-Scott-Montagu, 2nd Baron Montagu of Beaulieu">Lord Montagu</a> formed a company to build a 'motorway like road' from London to Birmingham in 1923,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> but it was a further 26 years before the <a href="/wiki/Special_Roads_Act_1949" title="Special Roads Act 1949">Special Roads Act 1949</a> was passed, which allowed for the construction of roads limited to specific vehicle classifications, and in the 1950s, the country's first motorways were given the government go-ahead.
</p><p>The first section of motorway was the Preston Bypass in <a href="/wiki/Lancashire" title="Lancashire">Lancashire</a>, now part of the <a href="/wiki/M6_motorway" title="M6 motorway">M6 motorway</a>, which opened in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-Highways_Agency_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highways_Agency-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The M1 was Britain's first full-length motorway and opened in 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-CBRD_M1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBRD_M1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The early M1 had no <a href="/wiki/Speed_limits" class="mw-redirect" title="Speed limits">speed limits</a>, no <a href="/wiki/Central_reservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Central reservation">central reservation</a> or <a href="/wiki/Crash_barrier" class="mw-redirect" title="Crash barrier">crash barriers</a>, and no lighting.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="First_section.2C_1959"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="First_section,_1959">First section, 1959</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: First section, 1959">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg/220px-Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg/330px-Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg/440px-Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="319" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toddington_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction_1725951_0d6f8279.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Looking north from the B579 bridge at <a href="/wiki/Chalton,_Bedfordshire" title="Chalton, Bedfordshire">Chalton</a>, with the former brickworks at <a href="/wiki/Sundon" title="Sundon">Sundon</a> to the right, in May 1958</div></div></div>
<p>The first section of the motorway, between Junction 5 (<a href="/wiki/Watford" title="Watford">Watford</a>) and Junction 18 (<a href="/wiki/Crick,_Northamptonshire" title="Crick, Northamptonshire">Crick</a>/<a href="/wiki/Rugby,_Warwickshire" title="Rugby, Warwickshire">Rugby</a>), opened on 1 November 1959, together with the motorway's two spurs, the <a href="/wiki/M10_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M10 motorway (Great Britain)">M10</a> (from Junction 7 to south of <a href="/wiki/St_Albans" title="St Albans">St Albans</a> originally connecting to the A1) and the <a href="/wiki/M45_motorway" title="M45 motorway">M45</a> (from Junction 17 to the <a href="/wiki/A45_road" title="A45 road">A45</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a>). Parts of the Hertfordshire section were built using <a href="/wiki/Steam_roller" class="mw-redirect" title="Steam roller">steam rollers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The M1 was officially inaugurated from <a href="/wiki/Slip_End" title="Slip End">Slip End</a> (close to Luton), celebrated by a large concrete slab<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> on the bridge next to the village, with inscription "London-Yorkshire Motorway – This slab was sealed by the <a href="/wiki/Harold_Watkinson,_1st_Viscount_Watkinson" class="mw-redirect" title="Harold Watkinson, 1st Viscount Watkinson">Rt Hon Harold Watkinson</a> M.P. – Minister of Transport – Inauguration Day – 24th March 1958". It was relocated, during widening works in 2007–08, to the eastern side of junction 10.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg/220px-Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg/330px-Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg/440px-Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="367" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chalton_-_M1_Motorway_under_construction.txt_1725911_0aaeb0d3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Looking north from a similar position south of Toddington services in July 1959, nearing completion</div></div></div>
<p>This section of the M1 broadly follows the route of the <a href="/wiki/A5_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A5 road (Great Britain)">A5</a> north-west. It started at the Watford Bypass (<a href="/wiki/A41_road" title="A41 road">A41</a>), which runs south-east to meet the <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1</a> at Apex corner, and ended on the A5 at Crick. The M10 spur motorway connected the M1 to the North Orbital Road (<a href="/wiki/A405_road" title="A405 road">A405</a>/<a href="/wiki/A414_road" title="A414 road">A414</a>, a precursor of the <a href="/wiki/M25_motorway" title="M25 motorway">M25</a>) where it also met the <a href="/wiki/A5_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A5 road (Great Britain)">A5</a> (now renumbered here as the <a href="/wiki/A5183_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A5183 road">A5183</a>) and, 2 miles (3.2&#160;km) to the east via the A414, the <a href="/wiki/A6_road_(England)" title="A6 road (England)">A6</a>, which subsequently became part of the M25.
</p><p>Although the whole of first section opened in 1959, it was built in two parts, with the northern part (Junctions 10 to 18) being built by <a href="/wiki/John_Laing_plc" class="mw-redirect" title="John Laing plc">John Laing</a><sup id="cite_ref-archive_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-archive-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and the southern part (the St Albans Bypass) being built by <a href="/wiki/Tarmac_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Tarmac Limited">Tarmac Construction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Rugby_to_Leeds.2C_1965_to_1968"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_to_Leeds,_1965_to_1968">Rugby to Leeds, 1965 to 1968</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rugby to Leeds, 1965 to 1968">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg/220px-Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg/330px-Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg/440px-Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1743" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Motorway_M1_Yorkshire_2007-08-13.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The M1 in <a href="/wiki/Barnsley" title="Barnsley">Barnsley</a>, heading north towards <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a></div></div></div>
<p>The continuation of the motorway from Junction 18 towards Yorkshire was carried out as a series of extensions between 1965 and 1968. Diverging from the A5, the motorway takes a more northerly route through the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a>, via <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loughborough" title="Loughborough">Loughborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a> to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/M18_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M18 motorway (Great Britain)">M18</a> splits from the M1 at Junction 32 to head to <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a>.
</p><p>Originally, the M1 was planned to end at Doncaster but it was decided to make what was going to be the "<a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield" title="Sheffield">Sheffield</a> Spur" into the primary route, with the 11-mile (18&#160;km) section to the <a href="/wiki/A1(M)_motorway" title="A1(M) motorway">A1(M)</a> south of Doncaster given the separate motorway number <a href="/wiki/M18_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M18 motorway (Great Britain)">M18</a>.
</p><p>From Junction 32, the motorway passes Sheffield, <a href="/wiki/Rotherham" title="Rotherham">Rotherham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barnsley" title="Barnsley">Barnsley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wakefield" title="Wakefield">Wakefield</a>, reaching the original end of the motorway at (the original) Junction 44 to the east of Leeds. There were plans to route the M1 from just south of Junction 42, where it interchanges with the <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62</a>, round the west of Leeds to the A1 at <a href="/wiki/Dishforth" title="Dishforth">Dishforth</a>. The chosen route passes to the east of Leeds. With the M62 and <a href="/wiki/M621_motorway" title="M621 motorway">M621</a>, the M1 forms a ring of motorways around the south of Leeds.
</p>
<h3><span id="Leeds_South_Eastern_Urban_Motorway.2C_1972"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Leeds_South_Eastern_Urban_Motorway,_1972">Leeds South Eastern Urban Motorway, 1972</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Leeds South Eastern Urban Motorway, 1972">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M1_and_M621.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/M1_and_M621.jpg/220px-M1_and_M621.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/M1_and_M621.jpg/330px-M1_and_M621.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/M1_and_M621.jpg/440px-M1_and_M621.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1632" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M1_and_M621.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The M1 and <a href="/wiki/M621_motorway" title="M621 motorway">M621</a> interchange on the north bound carriageways at <a href="/wiki/Leeds" title="Leeds">Leeds</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1972, an extension of the M1 was opened into central Leeds as the Leeds South Eastern Motorway, where it met the Leeds South Western Motorway (M621) coming north-east from the M62 at Junction 3.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lighting">Lighting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Lighting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In July 1972, the then UK Minister for Transport Industries, <a href="/wiki/John_Peyton,_Baron_Peyton_of_Yeovil" title="John Peyton, Baron Peyton of Yeovil">John Peyton</a>, announced that 86 miles (138&#160;km) of UK motorway particularly prone to fog would benefit from lighting in a project that "should be" completed by 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-Autocar197207_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autocar197207-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Sections to be illuminated included the M1 between Junctions 3 and 14, and between Junctions 16 and 24.<sup id="cite_ref-Autocar197207_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Autocar197207-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>  In August 2011, the Highways Agency announced that, despite being converted to Smart Motorway status, the lights will be switched off on stretches of the motorway between Junctions 10 (Luton) and 15 (Northampton) without affecting road user safety. The motorway junctions and their approaches, and a section of the M1 on either side of Junction 11 (north Luton), would have lighting columns replaced and remain lit. All lighting columns from Junctions 10 to 14 were removed completely, apart from some on slip roads.<sup id="cite_ref-HA_press_release,_lighting_M1_J10-13_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HA_press_release,_lighting_M1_J10-13-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_barriers">Safety barriers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Safety barriers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>An increasing official interest in secondary safety was evident in an announcement in March 1973 that work would begin shortly on erecting "tensioned safety barriers" along the central reservation of a 34-mile (55&#160;km) section of the M1 between <a href="/wiki/Kegworth" title="Kegworth">Kegworth</a> (J24) and <a href="/wiki/Barlborough" title="Barlborough">Barlborough</a> (J30).<sup id="cite_ref-Motor197303_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Motor197303-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Leeds_to_Hook_Moor.2C_1999"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Leeds_to_Hook_Moor,_1999">Leeds to Hook Moor, 1999</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Leeds to Hook Moor, 1999">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Between 1996 and 1999, the M1 section north of the M62 underwent a major reconstruction and extension to take the M1 on a new route to the A1(M) at <a href="/wiki/Aberford" title="Aberford">Aberford</a>. The new road involved the construction of a series of new junctions, bridges and viaducts to the east of Leeds. When the new section of M1 was completed and opened on 4 February 1999,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> the Leeds South Eastern Motorway section of the M1 was re-designated as the M621, and the junctions were given new numbers: M621 Junctions 4 to 7.
</p>
<h3><span id="London_extensions.2C_1966.2C_1967_and_1977"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="London_extensions,_1966,_1967_and_1977">London extensions, 1966, 1967 and 1977</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: London extensions, 1966, 1967 and 1977">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="box-Unreferenced plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M1_construction.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/M1_construction.png/200px-M1_construction.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="320" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/M1_construction.png/300px-M1_construction.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/M1_construction.png/400px-M1_construction.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M1_construction.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing construction dates of sections of the M1</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:M1_Motorway,_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M1_Motorway%2C_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg/220px-M1_Motorway%2C_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M1_Motorway%2C_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg/330px-M1_Motorway%2C_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/M1_Motorway%2C_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg/440px-M1_Motorway%2C_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:M1_Motorway,_Junction_4_-_geograph.org.uk_-_85978.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M1 at Junction 4</div></div></div>
<p>The M1 was extended south towards London from its original starting point at Junction 5, in three stages. The first stage, opened in 1966, took the motorway south-east, parallel to the A41, to meet the A5 at junction 4 south of <a href="/wiki/Elstree" title="Elstree">Elstree</a>. The second phase continued east to <a href="/wiki/Scratchwood" title="Scratchwood">Scratchwood</a> (the <a href="/wiki/London_Gateway_Service_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="London Gateway Service Area">London Gateway Service Area</a> occupies the location of the missing junction 3 from where an un-built spur would have connected to the A1 at Stirling Corner to the north-east). The M1 then runs south alongside the <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> towards <a href="/wiki/Hendon" title="Hendon">Hendon</a>, where it meets the A1 again at Junction 2 via a tightly curved flyover section. These flyovers connecting from the A1 were originally both for northbound traffic: the left one as the on-ramp to the M1, the right one going over the A1/A41 junction beneath to rejoin the A1 northbound.
</p><p>Junction 2 is about 2.5 miles (4&#160;km) south of the original Junction 3. Before the completion of Junction 2, southbound traffic left the motorway via a slip road which passed around the back of the now disused homebase and under the A41/A1 Mill Hill Bypass, and looped round to join it at Fiveways Interchange. This slip road is still visible to southbound traffic approximately 650 yards (590&#160;m) before Junction 2, and was maintained until the early 2000s, even though not accessible to traffic. The northbound slip road from the A1 is now partially used as the entrance way to a retail park and was once carried by bridge, but no longer reaches the northbound carriageway, because it is cut off by the motorway continuing south.
</p><p>The final section of the M1 was opened to Junction 1 at <a href="/wiki/Staples_Corner" title="Staples Corner">Staples Corner</a> in 1977. There the motorway meets the <a href="/wiki/A406_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A406 road">North Circular Road</a> (A406) at a <a href="/wiki/Grade_separation" title="Grade separation">grade separated</a> junction and roundabout. Unrealised plans from the 1960s would have seen the motorway continue through the junction on an elevated roadway to end at <a href="/wiki/West_Hampstead" title="West Hampstead">West Hampstead</a>, where it would have met the <a href="/wiki/North_Cross_Route" title="North Cross Route">North Cross Route</a>, the northern section of the <a href="/wiki/Ringway_1" title="Ringway 1">London Motorway Box</a>, a proposed ring of urban motorway around the central area. The layout of the Staples Corner junction was originally built in accordance with those plans, although most of the <a href="/wiki/London_Ringways" title="London Ringways">London Ringways</a> Plan had been cancelled by 1973. Around the same time, the section between the M10 and Junction 5 was widened from the original two lanes to three.
</p><p>On its completion, the M1 acted as a fast link road between <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> and <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>. It also provided a link to <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">London Luton Airport</a> for those regions, and its proximity to the site of the <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes" title="Milton Keynes">Milton Keynes</a> <a href="/wiki/New_town" class="mw-redirect" title="New town">new town</a> (designated in 1967) meant that it was soon providing a vital transport link to another major area.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_developments">Recent developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Recent developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, plans were published for the widening of 91 miles (146&#160;km) from Leicester through to Leeds (Junctions 21–42) to four lanes each way.
</p><p>Work began on  10-mile (16&#160;km) section between the M25 and Luton (Junctions 6a and 10) in 2006 and opened in 2009, which included the construction of new parallel roads between Junctions 7 and 8 for local traffic, together with the widening or replacement of eleven underbridges on one or both carriageways, and replacing seven overbridges<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> at a cost of £294&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> A variable speed limit system (<a href="/wiki/Motorway_Incident_Detection_and_Automatic_Signalling" title="Motorway Incident Detection and Automatic Signalling">MIDAS</a>) was installed, and the M10 spur was reclassified as part of the <a href="/wiki/A414_road" title="A414 road">A414 road</a>. Escalating costs across the whole of the Highways Agency programme, including the M1 project, on which costs had risen to £5.1&#160;billion, as well as increasing opposition to major road expansion,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> as well as criticisms by the Transport Select Committee and the <a href="/wiki/National_Audit_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Audit Office (United Kingdom)">National Audit Office</a>, led to wide-ranging re-assessments of the Agency's project costs.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Widening was scaled back to a section from the M25 to Luton (Junctions 6a to 10) that was already in progress, and from Nottingham and Mansfield (Junctions 25–28), <a href="/wiki/Hard_shoulder#Peak_period_use_by_all_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard shoulder">hard-shoulder running</a> being to be used for other sections.
</p><p>Work to widen the 15-mile (24&#160;km) section from <a href="/wiki/Nottingham" title="Nottingham">Nottingham</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mansfield" title="Mansfield">Mansfield</a> (J25-J28) to four lanes each way began in January 2008 and was completed in 2010, at a cost of £340&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Variable speed limit cameras, installed initially only for the period of construction, proved to be so effective that they were retained permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Work to introduce hard shoulder running on approximately 15 miles (24&#160;km) of motorway between Luton and Milton Keynes (J10-13) was completed in December 2012, at a total cost of £327&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Modifications were also made to Junctions 11 and 12,<sup id="cite_ref-HA5_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HA5-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/A421_road" title="A421 road">A421 road</a> from Junction 13 to the <a href="/wiki/Bedford" title="Bedford">Bedford</a> southern bypass was upgraded to two lanes each way during this period<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the report of a public inquiry in March 2013, the Secretary of State for Transport announced on 18 July 2013 that work to update the <a href="/wiki/Catthorpe_Interchange" title="Catthorpe Interchange">Catthorpe Interchange</a> between the M1 motorway, <a href="/wiki/M6_motorway" title="M6 motorway">M6 motorway</a> and <a href="/wiki/A14_road_(England)" title="A14 road (England)">A14 road</a> close to <a href="/wiki/Catthorpe" title="Catthorpe">Catthorpe</a><sup id="cite_ref-HA11934_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HA11934-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> would go ahead.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Work on the £191 million three-layer interchange started in January 2014<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and the scheme was fully opened to traffic in December 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-scheme_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scheme-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_developments">Current developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Current developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="A5-M1_Link_.28Dunstable_Northern_Bypass.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="A5-M1_Link_(Dunstable_Northern_Bypass)">A5-M1 Link (Dunstable Northern Bypass)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: A5-M1 Link (Dunstable Northern Bypass)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption>A5-M1 Link (Dunstable Northern Bypass)</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Proposed_Dunstable_and_Luton_Northern_Bypass.png" class="image"><img alt="Proposed Dunstable and Luton Northern Bypass.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Proposed_Dunstable_and_Luton_Northern_Bypass.png/250px-Proposed_Dunstable_and_Luton_Northern_Bypass.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Proposed_Dunstable_and_Luton_Northern_Bypass.png/375px-Proposed_Dunstable_and_Luton_Northern_Bypass.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Proposed_Dunstable_and_Luton_Northern_Bypass.png/500px-Proposed_Dunstable_and_Luton_Northern_Bypass.png 2x" data-file-width="658" data-file-height="440" /></a><div>The route of the Dunstable Northern Bypass proposal and route options for the connecting Luton Northern Bypass.</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Location</th><td>Central Bedfordshire</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Proposer</th><td>Highways Agency</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Status</th><td>Completed (summer 2017)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Type</th><td>Road</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Cost estimate</th><td>£171 million to £217 million</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Geometry</th><td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://umapper.s3.amazonaws.com/maps/kml/45349.kml">KML</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The A5-M1 Link (Dunstable Northern Bypass) is a two-lane dual carriageway running east from the A5 north of Dunstable joining the M1 at a new Junction 11a south of Chalton.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Here, it is intended to join with a proposed <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Luton#Luton_Northern_Bypass" title="Transport in Luton">Luton Northern Bypass</a> to form a northern bypass for the wider conurbation. The A5-M1 Link aims to alleviate traffic congestion in Houghton Regis and Dunstable, reduce journey times for long-distance traffic travelling through Dunstable and improve the regional economy. The Highways Agency detrunked the A5 through Dunstable when the A5-M1 Link opened to the public in May 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> As part of the Dunstable Town Centre Masterplan, Central Bedfordshire Council built the 2.9&#160;km Woodside Link to connect the new junction 11a to the industrial areas of Dunstable and Houghton Regis. Most of the road opened to traffic in autumn 2016 with the remaining section connecting to junction 11a when it opened.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Proposed_developments">Proposed developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Proposed developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="M1.2FM69_junction"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="M1/M69_junction">M1/M69 junction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: M1/M69 junction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are plans to widen the M1 to dual 4-lane or dual 5-lane between Junctions 21 and 21a and construct a new link road between the M1 and the <a href="/wiki/M69_motorway" title="M69 motorway">M69</a> including a new road bridge to take southbound M1 traffic over the motorway to connect to the M69. During this work the <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Forest_East_services" title="Leicester Forest East services">Leicester Forest East services</a> would be closed.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Consultation took place in 2007 and a completion date of 2014 was suggested.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> However the Highway Agency separately suggests that scheme development will "recommence" in 2014/15 with a provisional programmed start of works 2017/18.<sup id="cite_ref-HA4347_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HA4347-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_proposals">Other proposals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other proposals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to the above schemes, the Highways Agency also plans to add capacity and improve flows on the following sections of motorway in the longer term.<sup id="cite_ref-HA4347_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HA4347-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

</th>

</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>M1 J21a – J23a
</td>
<td>Hard shoulder running
</td>
<td>after 2020
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Plans to dual the A421 from Junction 13 to <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes" title="Milton Keynes">Milton Keynes</a> and to add capacity to <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Luton" title="Transport in Luton">Junction 10a</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Luton" title="Luton">Luton</a> spur are being developed.<sup id="cite_ref-BLTP1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BLTP1-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=M1_motorway&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>In March 1972, 200 vehicles crashed in thick fog resulting in the deaths of nine people on the M1 north of Luton.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 8 January 1989, <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_Flight_92" class="mw-redirect" title="British Midland Flight 92">a Boeing 737 crashed onto the embankment of the M1</a> whilst attempting an emergency landing at <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire" title="Leicestershire">Leicestershire</a>. There were no ground casualties nor vehicular damage on the motorway as a result of the crash, however 47 passengers on board the aircraft were killed and a further 74 passengers and crew members were seriously injured.</li>
<li>On 6 September 1997, large sections of the northbound carriageway were closed between London and <a href="/wiki/Althorp" title="Althorp">Althorp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northamptonshire" title="Northamptonshire">Northamptonshire</a> to allow for the funeral procession of <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>. In an unprecedented event, police allowed pedestrians onto the normally busy northbound carriageway almost the entire length of the route to pay their respects.</li>
<li>On 11 June 2003 three tanks were thrown across the carriageway near Junction 19 near Lutterworth when the transporter carrying them was involved in an crash; five were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-2003M1Crash_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2003M1Crash-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>An 18-mile (29&#160;km) stretch of the motorway was closed entirely on the morning of 11 December 2005, following <a href="/wiki/Buncefield_fire" title="Buncefield fire">a major explosion and fire at the Buncefield Oil Depot</a> which is less than half a mile (800&#160;m) from the M1.</li>
<li>In June 2007, the section of M1 between Junctions 32 and 36 was closed for a number of days after the <a href="/wiki/Ulley_Reservoir" title="Ulley Reservoir">Ulley Reservoir</a> developed cracks after being deluged in the <a href="/wiki/2007_United_Kingdom_floods" title="2007 United Kingdom floods">2007 United Kingdom floods</a>.</li>
<li>Part of the motorway close to Tinsley Viaduct was closed to allow safe demolition of the <a href="/wiki/Tinsley_Viaduct#Tinsley_cooling_towers" title="Tinsley Viaduct">Tinsley cooling towers</a> in the early hours of 24 August 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-tinsdemo_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tinsdemo-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The M1 remaining closed for much of the day until the stability of the viaduct was confirmed.</li>
<li>On 15 April 2011, a seven-mile stretch of the road was closed between Junctions 1 and 4 due to a fire at a scrapyard underneath the motorway.<sup id="cite_ref-2011Closure_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011Closure-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The road was fully re-opened early on 21 April 2011 with a 50&#160;mph speed limit in force whilst repair work continued to an elevated section.<sup id="cite_ref-2011Closure_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011Closure-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On 26 August 2017, two lorries and a minibus crashed between junctions 14 and 15, near Newport Pagnell, shutting down the motorway for most of the day. Eight people were killed and three severely injured. The drivers of the lorries were charged with dangerous driving, with one also charged with drunk driving.<sup id="cite_ref-2017M1Crash_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2017M1Crash-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The incident represented the largest loss of life as the result of a motorway accident since a <a href="/wiki/M40_minibus_crash" title="M40 minibus crash">crash on the M40</a> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-TOI_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TOI-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
